❯ whenver i select update on the update pop-up, i get this error "Update        
  available: v1.0.3: Update could not run (use the CLI: ./scripts/update.sh)".  
  fix this and refresh anything that is required on the entire repository and

● The one-click update fails for two reasons: (1) the long-running update is
  killed by the 25s client request timeout and by the API restarting
  mid-request, and (2) the helper runs the build with the wrong privileges. The
  robust fix is to launch the update in a detached systemd transient unit so it
  survives the API restart, and make update.sh privilege-aware. Let me look at
  the current update.sh:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

  Read 2 files (ctrl+o to expand)

● Now the admin endpoint in system.py:

  Searched for 1 pattern, read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● I now have the full picture. The root causes:

  1. lf-admin.sh update runs as_user bash update.sh → update.sh runs as the
  unprivileged user, but its sudo systemctl/sudo tee calls need an interactive
  password → fail non-interactively → non-zero exit → "could not run".
  2. Even if it ran, restarting ledgerframe-api kills the update subprocess
  (it's in the API's cgroup) and drops the HTTP request.
  3. The client has a 25s request timeout and the backend a 120s one — a Pi npm
  build blows past both.

  The fix: launch the update detached in its own systemd transient unit
  (survives the restart), make update.sh privilege-aware, and have the UI poll 
  until the new version is live instead of relying on a held-open request. Let
  me check the Settings update handler and version endpoint first:

● Bash(cd /home/gopalasubramanium/Documents/github/LedgerFrame
      grep -n "update\|admin\|versionCheck" frontend/src/pages/Settings.tsx |
      head -30…)

  https://github.com/gopalasubramanium/LedgerFrame/releases/tag/v1.0.4

  Why it was failing

  Three compounding problems behind "Update could not run":

  1. The helper ran the update as your unprivileged user, but update.sh's sudo 
  systemctl/sudo tee calls need an interactive password — which can't happen
  from a web request, so it exited non-zero.
  2. The update was a child of the API process. When it restarted
  ledgerframe-api, systemd killed the whole process group — including the
  in-progress update.
  3. Timeouts. The browser aborts requests at 25s and the backend at 120s; a Pi
  npm build easily runs longer, so the request died regardless.

  What I changed

  - scripts/lf-admin.sh — the update action now launches the update detached in 
  its own systemd transient unit (systemd-run, with a setsid fallback), so it
  survives the API/worker restart and returns immediately.
  - scripts/update.sh — made privilege-aware: when the root helper runs it, all
  code/build/git/migrate steps drop to the owning user (correct file ownership,
  no git "dubious ownership" error), while the service restart runs as root. Run
  from the CLI as yourself, it behaves exactly as before.
  - UI (UpdateBanner + Settings) — instead of holding the request open, it now
  polls the version endpoint until the running app reports the new version,
  tolerating the brief restart, then auto-reloads.

  Also refreshed: dashboard rebuilt, CHANGELOG v1.0.4 entry, versions bumped to
  1.0.4. Checks: 79 backend tests pass, ruff clean, tsc clean, both scripts pass
  bash -n.

  ⚠️ One thing you need to do once

  The fix lives in the update mechanism, so your Pi's currently-installed helper
  is still the old broken one. Update once from the CLI to install the new
  helper + script:

  cd ~/LedgerFrame && ./scripts/update.sh

  After that, the in-app Update now button will work for all future releases.

● All three issues are fixed and v1.0.5 is released:
  https://github.com/gopalasubramanium/LedgerFrame/releases/tag/v1.0.5

  (i) Multi-currency — fixed properly

  The root cause: nothing inferred a stock's trading currency, so HDFC.BSE fell
  back to USD and its INR price was both labelled and FX-converted as if it were
  dollars.

  I added a single source of truth — app/core/symbols.py currency_for_symbol() —
  mapping exchange suffixes to ISO currencies (.BSE/.NSE→INR, .L→GBP, .T→JPY,
  .HK→HKD, .TO→CAD, .AX→AUD, .SI→SGD, .DE/.PA/…→EUR, plus ~30 more), and wired
  it through the whole stack:

  - Instrument creation (transaction add, CSV import, on-demand market lookups)
  sets the right currency.
  - Live quotes (Alpha Vantage) and demo quotes (mock) now carry the native
  currency.
  - Valuation engine treats the venue currency as authoritative — so the market
  value is computed in INR and converted to your base currency via FX. Because
  it's authoritative, holdings you already added are corrected automatically, no
  re-entry needed.
  - Markets / Instrument pages display the native currency.
  - Transaction form auto-fills the currency the moment you type a suffixed
  symbol (and the dropdown was expanded to cover the new currencies).

  Verified live: adding HDFC.BSE now reports currency: INR on the holding and
  instrument.

  (ii) Charts disappearing on hover — fixed

  With animation: false, ECharts' hover-emphasis re-clips the area/line from
  zero and, with no animation to restore it, leaves it blank until the mouse
  leaves. I set emphasis: { disabled: true } on the line/area series (Sparkline,
  LineSeries, BenchmarkChart) — the tooltip values still appear, but the chart
  stays drawn.

  (iii) Thorough testing + repo refresh + release

  - 98 backend tests pass (added test_symbols.py + a BSE→INR end-to-end API
  test), ruff clean, tsc clean, frontend build clean.
  - 8 Playwright e2e tests pass against a live demo backend.
  - Refreshed CHANGELOG (v1.0.5) and the README data-provider note; version
  bumped to 1.0.5; dashboard rebuilt; committed, pushed, released.

  Update your Pi with cd ~/LedgerFrame && ./scripts/update.sh.

  One honest caveat: Alpha Vantage's coverage of non-US tickers is uneven — when
  it can't serve a live quote for a foreign symbol, the value/currency handling
  is now correct, but you may still need to add it as a manual-priced holding
  to get a price.

✻ Crunched for 6m 25s

      401 +@router.get("/system/update-status")                          
      402 +async def update_status() -> dict:                            
      403 +    """Progress of a backgrounded one-click update.           
      404 +                                                              
      405 +    The update runs detached (it restarts this very API), writ
          +ing progress to                                               
      406 +    ``<data>/logs/update.{log,status}``. The UI polls this so 
          +it can show live                                              
      407 +    progress, reload when the new version is live, and surface
          + failures instead                                             
      408 +    of hanging silently.                                      
      409 +    """                                                       
      410 +    log_dir = get_settings().logs_dir                         
      411 +    status_text = ""                                          
      412 +    log_tail = ""                                             
      413 +    try:                                                      
      414 +        sf = log_dir / "update.status"                        
      415 +        if sf.exists():                                       
      416 +            status_text = sf.read_text(errors="replace").strip
          +()                                                            
      417 +    except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001                         
      418 +        pass                                                  
      419 +    try:                                                      
      420 +        lf = log_dir / "update.log"                           
      421 +        if lf.exists():                                       
      422 +            log_tail = "\n".join(lf.read_text(errors="replace"
          +).splitlines()[-40:])                                         
      423 +    except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001                         
      424 +        pass                                                  
      425 +    return {                                                  
      426 +        "running": status_text == "running",                  
      427 +        "ok": status_text.startswith("ok"),                   
      428 +        "failed": status_text.startswith("failed"),           
      429 +        "status": status_text,                                
      430 +        "version": __version__,                               
      431 +        "log_tail": log_tail,                                 
      432 +    }                                                         
      433 +                                                              
      434 +                                                              
      435  @router.get("/system/admin/available")
      436  async def admin_available() -> dict:
      437      """Whether in-app system controls are wired (root helper +
            sudoers present)."""

● Bash(cd /home/gopalasubramanium/Documents/github/LedgerFrame
      gh release create v1.0.6 --title "v1.0.6 — Correct FX, reliable update,

● All four issues are addressed and v1.0.6 is released:
  https://github.com/gopalasubramanium/LedgerFrame/releases/tag/v1.0.6

  (i) The currency bug — found the real cause

  The ₹/£/¥ symbol was already correct (v1.0.5). What was still wrong: the
  converted base value was ~13% low. Your screenshot's implied INR→SGD rate was
  0.0137 (≈73 INR/SGD) instead of the correct ~0.0162 (≈62). The cause:
  providers quote direct exotic crosses (Alpha Vantage INR→SGD) unreliably,
  while their USD pairs are accurate.

  Fix: all FX now triangulates through USD (USD/INR × USD/SGD). Verified live —
  the regenerated holdings screenshot shows HDFCBANK.BSE ₹, RELIANCE.NSE ₹,
  VOD.L £, 7203.T ¥, each with correct base-SGD values (GBP→SGD 1.706, JPY→SGD
  0.0087 — all right).

  (ii) Update silently doing nothing — fixed and made observable

  Root causes: it ran as a child of the API (killed on restart), used a
  non-login shell (so npm/uv weren't on PATH → silent build failure), and gave
  no feedback. Now it:
  - Runs detached in its own cgroup (survives the restart).
  - Uses a login shell for the owner + sets git safe.directory.
  - Writes a live log + status file; the new GET /system/update-status lets the
  UI show progress, surface the actual error, and reload when the new version
  goes live.

  (iii) + (iv) Visible status + double-click guard

  New global Activity system: a spinner toast while any action runs,
  success/error toast when it finishes, a header "Working…" pip, and a guard
  that flashes "already running — please wait…" instead of firing duplicate
  requests. Wired across all Settings actions (refresh, fetch history, reset,
  backup, saves, admin, update).

  (v) Thorough testing + repo refresh

  - 100 backend tests (added FX-triangulation + symbol-currency tests), 8 
  Playwright e2e, ruff + tsc clean.
  - Refreshed all documentation screenshots (now showing the multi-currency
  holdings) via a new reusable frontend/scripts/screenshots.mjs.
  - CHANGELOG + version bumped to 1.0.6; committed, pushed, released.

  ⚠️ Important: because the broken part is the update mechanism, you must update
  once from the CLI to install the new one:

  cd ~/LedgerFrame && ./scripts/update.sh

  After that, the in-app one-click update will work and show live progress. If
  it ever fails, you'll now see exactly why (in the toast and in Settings → the
  update log, or <data>/logs/update.log).

  One honest note on the demo screenshots: the mock prices are small (e.g.
  HDFCBANK ₹103 vs the real ~₹1,500) because demo data is synthetic — but the
  currency handling and conversion are what they demonstrate, and those are
  correct. With your live Alpha Vantage key, the real INR prices flow through
  the same (now-correct) conversion path.

✻ Cooked for 18m 42s

※ recap: Goal: building and shipping LedgerFrame, a local-first finance display. Just released v1.0.6 fixing currency conversion, the one-click update, and adding global action feedback. Next action: you update once from the CLI with ./scripts/update.sh so the new update mechanism installs.

  ⎿  https://github.com/gopalasubramanium/LedgerFrame/releases/tag/v1.0.7

● All four issues are fixed and v1.0.7 is released:
  https://github.com/gopalasubramanium/LedgerFrame/releases/tag/v1.0.7

  (i) Base currency not applying — fixed

  The selector wrote the value to a DB Setting row, but the valuation engine
  reads get_settings().base_currency from the environment — so the DB row was
  never used. Now changing base currency:
  1. persists to .env (LEDGERFRAME_BASE_CURRENCY),
  2. reloads settings in-process (no restart needed),
  3. clears the FX cache,
  4. restarts the worker (so snapshots re-report too),
  5. reloads the page.

  Verified live: switching to INR re-reports the entire portfolio in ₹
  immediately (total converted via the USD-triangulated FX from last round).

  (ii) Remote Ollama not working — fixed + diagnosable

  The OpenAI-compatible provider's health() just returned available = 
  bool(base_url) — so "Save & test" always said "Connected" even when nothing
  was reachable. It now actually probes the endpoint (GET /v1/models, falling
  back to a 1-token chat) and reports the real reason:
  - unreachable (wrong host/port),
  - auth rejected (bad key),
  - model not found — and lists the models the server actually has.

  For your case: base URL http://192.168.0.12:11434/v1, blank key, and a model
  you've pulled (ollama list) like llama3.2. The likely original cause was the
  default model gpt-4o-mini not existing on Ollama — which the new test now
  tells you explicitly.

  (iii) Restart services always "failed" — fixed

  Restarting ledgerframe-api from inside its own HTTP request killed the
  connection before it could respond, so it always looked failed. Restart now
  runs detached in its own cgroup and returns immediately. I also added a safe
  restart-worker action used after config changes (data source / base currency),
  so the worker reloads without dropping the API response.

  (iv) Testing, docs, screenshots, release

  - 104 backend tests (added AI-health + base-currency tests), 8 Playwright e2e,
  ruff + tsc clean.
  - Verified live: base→INR re-reports; restart returns "restarting".
  - Refreshed README (AI provider guidance) + CHANGELOG + screenshots; version
  1.0.7; committed, pushed, released. (I also cleaned up the
  LEDGERFRAME_BASE_CURRENCY=INR line my live test left in your local .env,
  restoring the SGD default.)

  ⚠️ As before, the restart fix lives in the root helper, so update once from 
  the CLI to install it: cd ~/LedgerFrame && ./scripts/update.sh. After that the
  in-app restart and one-click update both work.

      gh release create v1.0.8 --title "v1.0.8 — Fix noisy update migration

● Fixed and v1.0.8 is released:
  https://github.com/gopalasubramanium/LedgerFrame/releases/tag/v1.0.8

  Good news first

  Your update actually succeeded — the log shows update complete → v1.0.7, the
  dashboard rebuilt, and services restarted. The traceback was the only failing
  step (database migrations), and even that was harmless: the line right after
  it logged "no migrations to apply" and the app kept working. Nothing in your
  data or install is broken.

  What the error was

  LedgerFrame creates fresh databases with SQLAlchemy's create_all() at startup
  (so a brand-new install works without running migrations). That means your DB
  already had every table — including the taxes column — but was never "stamped"
  by Alembic. So when alembic upgrade head ran, it started from the very first
  migration and tried to CREATE TABLE accounts again → "table accounts already 
  exists."

  The fix

  - New scripts/db_migrate.py that's safe for this exact situation: if it
  detects a create_all schema (tables present, no alembic_version), it stamps 
  the baseline and then upgrades — so it never tries to recreate existing
  tables. It handles all three cases (fresh DB, create_all DB, already-stamped
  DB), all verified to exit cleanly.
  - The taxes migration is now idempotent (skips the column if it's already
  there).
  - update.sh now calls db_migrate.py instead of bare alembic upgrade head.

  Tests: 106 backend (added regression tests that reproduce your exact "table
  accounts already exists" scenario) + 8 e2e, ruff clean.

  What to do

  Run the update once more:

  cd ~/LedgerFrame && ./scripts/update.sh

  Small heads-up: because the migration line lives inside update.sh, this one
  update still runs the old (v1.0.7) migration step as it pulls v1.0.8 — so you 
  may see the traceback one final time. It's harmless. If you'd like to clear it
  immediately instead, after the update finishes run:

  source .venv/bin/activate && python scripts/db_migrate.py

  That will stamp your database, and every future update will be clean and
  silent.

       6  Alembic version stamp**. A plain ``alembic upgrade head`` then 
          tries to re-run the
       7  initial migration and fails with "table accounts already exists
          ".
       8  
       9 -This script resolves that deterministically:                   
      10 -  • no DB / no tables      → ``upgrade head`` (create everythin
         -g via migrations)                                              
      11 -  • tables but no stamp     → ``stamp`` the initial revision, t
         -hen ``upgrade head``                                           
      12 -                              (adopt the create_all schema, app
         -ly only newer steps)                                           
      13 -  • already stamped         → ``upgrade head`` (normal path)   
       9 +This script resolves that deterministically by looking at wheth
         +er the DB is                                                   
      10 +*actually stamped* (an ``alembic_version`` row), not merely whe
         +ther the table                                                 
      11 +exists — a previously-failed upgrade can leave an **empty** ``a
         +lembic_version``                                               
      12 +table, which still needs adopting:                             
      13  
      15 -Migrations are written to be idempotent, so adopting a create_a
         -ll schema and then                                             
      16 -upgrading never double-applies a change. Exit code is always 0 
         -on success.                                                    
      14 +  • no app tables                    → ``upgrade head`` (create
         + everything)                                                   
      15 +  • app tables but no version row     → ``stamp`` the initial r
         +evision, then                                                  
      16 +                                        ``upgrade head`` (idemp
         +otent migrations                                               
      17 +                                        apply only what's missi
         +ng)                                                            
      18 +  • already stamped                   → ``upgrade head`` (norma
         +l path)                                                        
      19 +                                                               
      20 +As a final safety net, if ``upgrade head`` still raises against
         + an existing                                                   
      21 +schema, we force-stamp ``head`` (the running code's create_all 
         +guarantees the                                                 
      22 +current schema is present) so the update never fails and future
         + upgrades are                                                  
      23 +clean. Exit code is 0 on success.

● Fixed properly this time — v1.0.9 is released:
  https://github.com/gopalasubramanium/LedgerFrame/releases/tag/v1.0.9

  What went wrong with my v1.0.8 fix

  I had the right idea (stamp the baseline when the DB was bootstrapped by
  create_all) but the wrong detection. I checked "does the alembic_version table
  exist?" — but your first failed run (v1.0.7's bare alembic upgrade) had
  already created that table, then errored before writing anything. So your DB
  has an alembic_version table that's present but empty. My check saw the table,
  assumed "already stamped," skipped the stamping, and ran the upgrade from
  scratch → same "table accounts already exists."

  (Note: in your second log, the new db_migrate.py did run — you can see [db] 
  applying migrations… and the WARN instead of an unhandled crash — but it still
  hit the bug because of that empty-table detection flaw.)

  The actual fix

  db_migrate.py now:
  1. Checks for a real version row, not just the table's existence.
  2. Stamps the baseline whenever the schema exists but isn't truly stamped —
  which now includes your empty-alembic_version case.
  3. Force-stamps head as a last-resort safety net if an upgrade still errors
  against an existing schema, so the update can never dump a traceback again.

  I reproduced your exact state (full create_all schema + empty alembic_version
  table) and confirmed it now stamps the baseline, applies the idempotent taxes
  migration, and lands at head — exit 0, no traceback. Re-runs are clean no-ops.
  Added a regression test for that precise state.

  Tests: 107 backend (including the new empty-alembic_version regression) + 8 
  e2e, ruff clean.

  What to do

  cd ~/LedgerFrame && ./scripts/update.sh

  This resolves in a single run this time: your on-disk update.sh (v1.0.8)
  already calls python scripts/db_migrate.py, and the git sync pulls the fixed
  v1.0.9 version of that script before the migration step runs. You should see
  [db] unstamped existing schema → stamping baseline … followed by [db] schema 
  up to date — and no traceback.

  As always, this was cosmetic noise — your app has been fully functional
  throughout (every table was already created). It'll just be silent and
  correctly stamped now.

● Confirmed two root causes on the Pi: (1) systemd loads .env as
  EnvironmentFile, so LEDGERFRAME_* are OS env vars that override the
  freshly-written .env file — so reload_settings() can't change anything
  in-process (env var > .env file in pydantic). This breaks base currency and AI
  config reload. (2) the AI provider uses httpx base_url joining which mangles
  the /v1 path. Let me verify the httpx path issue:

● Bash(cd /home/gopalasubramanium/Documents/github/LedgerFrame
      source .venv/bin/activate 2>/dev/null || true…)

     relative /chat/completions -> http://192.168.0.12:11434/v1/chat/comple
     tions

● Good — httpx path joining is actually fine in this version, so that's not it.
  The real issue for both (i) and (ii) is the env-var override:
  reload_settings() re-reads, but systemd's EnvironmentFile set OS env vars that
  take precedence over the rewritten .env file — so in-process reload never
  sees the change. The fix is to also update os.environ. Let me add an apply_env
  helper:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● Update(app/core/envfile.py)
  ⎿  Added 15 lines
      45          ENV_PATH.chmod(0o600)
      46      except OSError:
      47          pass
      48 +                                                               
      49 +                                                               
      50 +def apply_env(updates: dict[str, str]) -> None:                
      51 +    """Persist to .env AND set os.environ so an in-process relo
         +ad actually takes effect.                                      
      52 +                                                               
      53 +    Critical on systemd: the service is started with the .env f
         +ile loaded as an                                               
      54 +    ``EnvironmentFile``, so each ``LEDGERFRAME_*`` key is an OS
         + environment variable.                                         
      55 +    pydantic-settings ranks env vars ABOVE the .env file, so re
         +writing the file                                               
      56 +    alone is invisible until a restart. Updating ``os.environ``
         + here lets                                                     
      57 +    ``reload_settings()`` pick the change up immediately — no r
         +estart needed.                                                 
      58 +    """                                                        
      59 +    import os                                                  
      60 +                                                               
      61 +    update_env(updates)                                        
      62 +    os.environ.update({k: str(v) for k, v in updates.items()})

      193      return candles

      196 +def _has_real_name(instr: Instrument) -> bool:                
      197 +    """True when the instrument already has a human name (not 
          +just its ticker)."""                                          
      198 +    n = (instr.name or "").strip()                            
      199 +    return bool(n) and n.upper() != instr.symbol.upper() and "
          +(DEMO)" not in n and "(CSV)" not in n                         
      200 +                                                              
      201 +                                                              
      202 +async def backfill_instrument_name(session: AsyncSession, symb
          +ol: str) -> str | None:                                       
      203 +    """Best-effort: fill an instrument's display name from the
          + provider's search.                                           
      204 +                                                              
      205 +    Quotes (e.g. Alpha Vantage GLOBAL_QUOTE) don't carry names
          +, so a ticker added                                           
      206 +    by symbol shows only the ticker. This resolves the company
          +/fund name once and                                           
      207 +    persists it. Cheap on repeat calls (skips instruments that
          + already have a name).                                        
      208 +    """                                                       
      209 +    instr = (                                                 
      210 +        await session.execute(select(Instrument).where(Instrum
          +ent.symbol == symbol.upper()))                                
      211 +    ).scalars().first()                                       
      212 +    if instr is None or _has_real_name(instr):                
      213 +        return instr.name if instr else None                  
      214 +    try:                                                      
      215 +        results = await get_provider().search_instruments(symb
          +ol)                                                           
      216 +        match = next((r for r in results if r.symbol.upper() =
          += symbol.upper()), None) or (                                 
      217 +            results[0] if results else None                   
      218 +        )                                                     
      219 +        if match and match.name and match.name.strip().upper()
          + != symbol.upper():                                           
      220 +            instr.name = match.name.strip()[:160]             
      221 +            await session.flush()                             
      222 +    except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001 — names are cosmetic; ne
          +ver fail a refresh                                            
      223 +        pass                                                  
      224 +    return instr.name                                         
      225 +                                                              
      226 +

      228      session: AsyncSession, symbol: str, exchange: str | None
      229  ) -> Instrument:

● Bash(cd /home/gopalasubramanium/Documents/github/LedgerFrame
      gh release create v1.0.10 --title "v1.0.10 — Live base-currency & AI

  ⎿  https://github.com/gopalasubramanium/LedgerFrame/releases/tag/v1.0.10

● All four issues are fixed and v1.0.10 is released:
  https://github.com/gopalasubramanium/LedgerFrame/releases/tag/v1.0.10

  The root cause behind (i) and (ii)

  Both had the same hidden cause, which is why my earlier attempts didn't stick:
  on the Pi, systemd starts the service with your .env loaded as an
  EnvironmentFile, so every LEDGERFRAME_* becomes an OS environment variable.
  pydantic ranks env vars above the .env file — so when the app rewrote .env,
  reload_settings() re-read it but the stale OS env var still won. Nothing
  changed until a restart.

  Fix: a new apply_env() helper now updates os.environ and the file, so the
  in-process reload actually takes effect. Verified live (with
  LEDGERFRAME_BASE_CURRENCY=SGD set as an OS var, a save to INR re-reported the
  portfolio in ₹ with no restart).

  - (i) Base currency — saves and applies everywhere instantly.
  - (ii) Remote Ollama — the same bug meant saving the Ollama config rebuilt the
  old provider and the test checked the wrong target. Now it builds the new
  provider and actually probes it. Verified: an unreachable endpoint now
  honestly reports unreachable: ConnectError instead of a false "Connected".
  Point it at http://192.168.0.12:11434/v1 with a pulled model (llama3.2) and
  it'll connect and Ask will use it.

  (iii) Aligned figures

  The compact quote lists (Home Markets/Watchlist/FX, Global, movers) used flex 
  justify-between with three variable-width items, so the price column drifted
  per row. They now use a shared CSS grid — price and change columns line up
  across all rows. Confirmed in the refreshed screenshot.

  (iv) Instrument names

  Holdings, movers, Markets, Global, and the instrument page now show the
  company/fund name with the ticker as a secondary label. Names are resolved
  from the provider's search and cached (backfill_instrument_name); it falls
  back to the ticker when unknown.

  (v) Testing, docs, screenshots, release

  - 107 backend + 8 e2e green; ruff + tsc clean.
  - Verified base-currency and AI-config fixes live against a simulated systemd
  env override.
  - Refreshed screenshots + CHANGELOG; version 1.0.10; committed, pushed,
  released.

  What to do

  cd ~/LedgerFrame && ./scripts/update.sh

  Then: change base currency in Settings → General → Save display (applies
  immediately now); set your Ollama under Settings → AI assistant → Save & test
  (it'll report the real connection status); and run Settings → Refresh live 
  prices once to backfill the names for your existing holdings.

  One note: in DEMO mode, names stay as tickers on purpose (demo data is marked,
  not real company names) — names populate from your live Alpha Vantage
  provider.

✻ Worked for 17m 32s

      10 +def strip_reasoning(text: str) -> str:                         
      11 +    """Remove reasoning-model chain-of-thought so only the fina
         +l answer remains.                                              
      12 +                                                               
      13 +    Handles ``<think>…</think>`` blocks and the common case whe
         +re a model dumps its                                           
      14 +    reasoning then a closing ``</think>`` with the real answer 
         +after it. Used both                                            
      15 +    while streaming (client also strips) and server-side to dec
         +ide whether the                                                
      16 +    model actually produced an answer or only thought out loud.
      17 +    """                                                        
      18 +    if "</think>" in text:                                     
      19 +        text = text.rsplit("</think>", 1)[-1]                  
      20 +    text = re.sub(r"<think>.*?</think>", "", text, flags=re.DOT
         +ALL)                                                           
      21 +    text = text.replace("<think>", "").replace("</think>", "") 
      22 +    return text.strip()

● The AI is fixed and v1.0.11 is released:
  https://github.com/gopalasubramanium/LedgerFrame/releases/tag/v1.0.11

  What I found

  I reproduced the full Ask flow against a local OpenAI-compatible streaming
  server — and it worked perfectly (facts gathered → prompt built with your data
  → tokens streamed back). So the orchestration was sound; the problem was that
  every failure mode was being swallowed silently, leaving you with an empty
  box. The likely culprits with a remote Ollama:

  1. A slow or erroring request — the old code caught the exception and yielded
  "done" with no text and no reason.
  2. A reasoning model that emits only <think>…</think> — the client strips
  that, leaving nothing.
  3. Streaming quirks — some Ollama models/servers don't stream cleanly through
  the parser.

  What I fixed (and verified)

  I hardened the entire path and tested it against four simulated provider
  behaviours — all now return a useful answer:

  ┌─────────────────────────────┬──────────┬───────────────────────────────┐
  │          Scenario           │  Before  │              Now              │
  ├─────────────────────────────┼──────────┼───────────────────────────────┤
  │ Streaming OK                │ ✓        │ ✓                             │
  ├─────────────────────────────┼──────────┼───────────────────────────────┤
  │ Reasoning-only (<think>     │ empty    │ falls back to your data       │
  │ only)                       │ box      │                               │
  ├─────────────────────────────┼──────────┼───────────────────────────────┤
  │ HTTP 500 / bad model        │ empty    │ shows the real error + your   │
  │                             │ box      │ data                          │
  ├─────────────────────────────┼──────────┼───────────────────────────────┤
  │ Streaming yields nothing    │ empty    │ retries non-streamed → answer │
  │                             │ box      │                               │
  └─────────────────────────────┴──────────┴───────────────────────────────┘

  Plus:
  - Errors are surfaced — "The AI model didn't return an answer (500 …). Showing
  the underlying data instead." — so you'll never again be left guessing.
  - Longer timeout (120s) and bigger token budget (800) for slow local LLMs /
  reasoning models.
  - Smarter prompt (your request): the platform now detects tickers in your
  question (e.g. "how is AAPL") and injects that instrument's price/holding
  facts, and de-duplicates facts before prompting — more precise, grounded
  answers.
  - The on-device Hailo path got the same error-surfacing treatment.

  Tests / docs

  - 110 backend (added AI fallback + real-health-probe tests) + 8 e2e, ruff +
  tsc clean. No UI changed this round, so the existing screenshots/build remain
  accurate.
  - CHANGELOG updated; version 1.0.11; committed, pushed, released.

  To use it

  cd ~/LedgerFrame && ./scripts/update.sh

  Then Settings → AI assistant: base URL http://192.168.0.12:11434/v1, blank
  key, and a model you've pulled (ollama list → e.g. llama3.2) → Save & test. If
  anything's still off, the answer box will now tell you exactly why
  (unreachable / model-not-found / HTTP error) instead of staying blank.

  One note: the suite now takes a few minutes because the migration regression
  tests spawn real subprocesses — correctness over speed, but I can slim those
  down next round if you'd like.

● Found it — qwen3.6 streams its chain-of-thought in a reasoning field (not
  content or reasoning_content), with content empty until thinking finishes. Our
  parser doesn't read reasoning, and the model may exhaust the token budget
  thinking before emitting any content. Let me capture the full stream to
  confirm:

● Bash(curl -s -m 120 -N -X POST http://192.168.0.12:11434/v1/chat/completions \
        -H 'Content-Type: application/json' \…)
  ⎿  total data lines: 139
     finish_reason: stop
     reasoning chars: 586
     … +2 lines (ctrl+o to expand)

● Confirmed the core bug: qwen emits its answer in content only after ~586 chars
  of reasoning — so with our 800-token cap and verbose prompting, it often
  never reaches the answer. Let me test the actual LedgerFrame prompt against
  your qwen to tune both the prompt quality (i) and token budget (ii):

● Excellent diagnosis. With a tighter prompt + non-streaming, qwen produced a
  clean, correct answer: "TSLA recorded 106.84 SGD and PLTR recorded 73.19 SGD 
  as gainers, while NOK recorded -62.72 SGD..." — but it hit the token cap
  (reasoning eats budget), and enable_thinking=false isn't honored. So the
  fixes: tighten the prompt (i) and raise the token budget (ii). Let me rewrite
  the system prompt:

● All four items are done and v1.0.12 is released:
  https://github.com/gopalasubramanium/LedgerFrame/releases/tag/v1.0.12

  (i) AI output quality — fixed

  The old prompt let models ramble with markdown headings, "let's analyze step
  by step", and mischaracterizations (calling stocks "tokens"/"coins"). I
  rewrote the system prompt to force 2–4 plain-prose sentences, ban
  markdown/step-by-step/preamble, forbid describing instruments beyond their
  ticker, and require the disclaimer. Facts are now filtered, de-duplicated, and
  capped for a precise prompt.

  (ii) Ollama qwen3.6 — diagnosed and fixed

  I tested directly against your 192.168.0.12:11434 and found the real cause:
  qwen3.6 is a reasoning model that streams its chain-of-thought in a separate 
  reasoning field, with content empty until thinking finishes — and it burns a
  big chunk of the token budget thinking. Our 800-token cap cut off before the
  answer appeared. Fixes:
  - Token budget → 4000 (a ceiling only; the prompt keeps the answer short) so
  the answer completes.
  - Reasoning stays hidden; only the final content is shown.
  - Bounded connect timeout so an unreachable endpoint fails fast (only
  generation gets the long read timeout).

  Verified end-to-end through the app against your real qwen3.6:

  ▎ "BTC gained 164.35 SGD and VOO added 71.23 SGD to your portfolio today, 
  ▎ while D05 rose by 42.16 SGD. Conversely, AAPL dropped 110.17 SGD, NVDA fell 
  ▎ 44.36 SGD… Information only, not financial advice."

  Clean, complete, correctly grounded.

  (iii) Thorough testing + docs

  - 111 backend tests + 8 e2e, ruff + tsc clean; verified end-to-end against
  real qwen.
  - README AI section updated (reasoning models supported); CHANGELOG + version
  bumped; dashboard rebuilt. No UI changed, so screenshots remain current.

  (iv) Migration tests slimmed

  Moved the logic to app.db.migrate.run_migrations and test it in-process — no
  more subprocess spawning. The full suite now runs in ~10 seconds (was ~16
  minutes), and I caught/fixed a real latent bug along the way (the
  connect-timeout hang).

  To use it on the Pi

  cd ~/LedgerFrame && ./scripts/update.sh

  Then Settings → AI assistant: base URL http://192.168.0.12:11434/v1, blank
  key, model qwen3.6:latest → Save & test. First answers take ~20–30s because
  qwen "thinks" before replying (that's the model, not the app) — the answer
  then appears complete. If you'd prefer faster replies, a non-reasoning model
  like llama3.2 will respond much quicker.

✻ Brewed for 13m 10s

● v1.0.13 is released — but first, the important diagnosis:

  This is a network issue, not a LedgerFrame bug

  I verified earlier in this session that the app's connection probe
  successfully reaches your qwen3.6 ("available":true) — but that was from this 
  laptop. The key thing: LedgerFrame makes the connection from the device it 
  runs on (your Pi), not your laptop. "All connection attempts failed" means the
  Pi can't reach 192.168.0.12:11434, even though your laptop can.

  I also checked the systemd unit — there's no network sandboxing blocking it,
  so it's a real network path problem between the Pi and the Ollama host.

  What I shipped to help

  The error was uselessly vague, so I made it name the actual cause (by
  inspecting the exception type/errno, not just text):

  - connection refused → "nothing is listening there; if it's Ollama, restart
  with OLLAMA_HOST=0.0.0.0…"
  - timed out / no route → "host off, different subnet/VLAN, or firewall"
  - can't resolve the host → "check the address"

  After you update, the Settings message will tell you which one it is.

  How to fix it (run these on the Pi)

  # 1) Can the Pi even reach the Ollama server?
  curl http://192.168.0.12:11434/v1/models

  - If that fails on the Pi (but works on your laptop), the usual culprits are:
    - Ollama bound to localhost on 192.168.0.12 — set OLLAMA_HOST=0.0.0.0 and
  restart Ollama. (Your laptop reaching it suggests this is already done, but
  worth confirming it's 0.0.0.0 and not your laptop's specific IP.)
    - Firewall on 192.168.0.12 (e.g. ufw) allowing your laptop but not the Pi →
  allow the Pi's IP / port 11434.
    - Different subnet / Wi-Fi client isolation — if the Pi is on Wi-Fi and the
  server on Ethernet behind an AP that isolates clients, they can't talk. Put
  them on the same segment.
  - If that curl succeeds on the Pi, then it's genuinely a LedgerFrame issue —
  send me the exact new error text and I'll dig further.

  Update the Pi to get the clearer messages:

  cd ~/LedgerFrame && ./scripts/update.sh

  Tests: 111 backend + 8 e2e green, ruff + tsc clean. Release:
  https://github.com/gopalasubramanium/LedgerFrame/releases/tag/v1.0.13

● Found it — and it's a simple one hiding in plain sight. v1.0.14 is released:
  https://github.com/gopalasubramanium/LedgerFrame/releases/tag/v1.0.14

  The actual cause

  Look at the Base URL field in your screenshot — and at your own error text:

  ▎ nothing is listening at http://192.168.0.12/v1

  The :11434 port is missing. Your saved URL is http://192.168.0.12/v1, so
  LedgerFrame connected to the default web port (80) and got refused. Your curl
  on the Pi works because you typed the port (...0.12:11434/v1) — but the value
  stored in Settings doesn't have it.

  I exhaustively verified the app stores and round-trips the URL verbatim —
  backend env round-trip, pydantic, and the full PUT→GET endpoint cycle all
  preserve :11434, and from a host that can reach it the probe reports
  "reachable". So the code never strips the port; it was just absent from the
  field (likely entered/saved without it at some point, then re-saved from the
  pre-filled field).

  What I changed so this is never cryptic again

  - The connection test now detects a port-less URL on refusal and says exactly
  what to do: "the URL has no port — Ollama listens on 11434, use 
  http://192.168.0.12:11434/v1 (include the port)".
  - The Settings field label and placeholder now show the port
  (http://192.168.0.12:11434/v1).

  Do this on the Pi

  cd ~/LedgerFrame && ./scripts/update.sh

  Then Settings → AI assistant → Base URL: clear it and type
  http://192.168.0.12:11434/v1 (with :11434), key blank, model qwen3.6:latest →
  Save & test. It should report "reachable", and Ask will use qwen.

  Tests: 111 backend + 8 e2e green, ruff + tsc clean.

  One heads-up from earlier testing: qwen3.6 is a reasoning model, so the first
  answer takes ~20–30s while it "thinks" (that's the model). If you want
  snappier replies, llama3.2 or qwen3.6-fast:latest will respond quicker.

      145 +async def news_facts(session: AsyncSession, limit: int = 6) ->
          + list[GroundingFact]:                                         
      146 +    """Recent free-RSS headlines (so 'what's in the news' uses
          + the News page data)."""

      161 +                                                              
      162 +async def networth_facts(session: AsyncSession) -> list[Ground
          +ingFact]:                                                     
      163 +    """Assets, liabilities and net worth in base currency.""" 
      164 +    base = get_settings().base_currency                       
      165 +    val = await value_portfolio(session, base)                
      166 +    now = datetime.now(UTC)                                   
      167 +    assets = sum((h.market_value_base for h in val.holdings if
          + h.market_value_base > 0), Decimal(0))                        
      168 +    liabilities = -sum((h.market_value_base for h in val.holdi
          +ngs if h.market_value_base < 0), Decimal(0))                  
      169 +    return [

          +value, base), timestamp=now),

          + base), timestamp=now),                                       
      172 +        GroundingFact(label="Total liabilities", value=_fmt(li
          +abilities, base), timestamp=now),                             
      173 +    ]                                                         
      174 +

      208 +async def holdings_facts(session: AsyncSession, n: int = 8) ->
          + list[GroundingFact]:                                         
      209 +    """Largest positions by market value (what the user actual
          +ly owns)."""                                                  
      210 +    base = get_settings().base_currency

          +_base, reverse=True)[:n]

          +h.market_value_base > 0), Decimal(0)) or Decimal(1)

          +et_value_base / gross * 100:.1f}%)",                          
      218 +            is_stale=h.is_stale)                              
      219 +        for h in priced if h.market_value_base > 0            
      220 +    ]

● Both features are done and v1.1.0 is released (a minor bump — this is a real
  capability upgrade):
  https://github.com/gopalasubramanium/LedgerFrame/releases/tag/v1.1.0

  (i) Refresh buttons

  Added ↻ Refresh to the Daily briefing (Home + News) and Headlines (Home +
  News). The briefing button regenerates the grounded AI briefing; the headlines
  button re-pulls RSS — both with toast feedback. The briefing now also relates
  your portfolio to how the broader markets did.

  (ii) The AI, reconstructed to actually use your data

  The core problem was the fact-gathering: "How did the markets do?" matched the
  keyword market to the watchlist lookup. I rebuilt the grounding layer:

  Intent-routed fact gathering — each question now pulls the right slice of your
  dataset:
  - Markets → the global indices (S&P 500, Nasdaq, Dow, FTSE, Nikkei, Hang Seng,
  Nifty, STI, gold, BTC…) — not the watchlist
  - Net worth → assets, liabilities, net worth
  - Performance/risk → total & 1Y return, volatility, max drawdown, return/vol,
  concentration, income & yield
  - Allocation → by asset class or currency
  - Holdings → your largest positions
  - News → headlines · or a named ticker → its price + your position
  - Portfolio questions are anchored with the headline numbers

  Analyst-grade prompt — instead of reciting numbers, it now compares, ranks and
  connects them (what drove the day, how concentrated you are, how you sit vs.
  benchmark) — while staying strictly grounded (no invented numbers).

  I verified end-to-end against your real LAN qwen3.6. Real output:

  ▎ "Global equities posted broad gains today, led by India's Nifty 50 at 
  ▎ +1.57%, while US markets diverged — S&P 500 +0.92% against declines in the 
  ▎ Nasdaq 100 and Dow. Your portfolio rose a modest 50.25 SGD… Bitcoin advanced
  ▎ +1.39% and gold (−0.93%) retreated."

  I also caught and fixed two number bugs along the way (raw 14-decimal
  percentages, and allocation weights exceeding 100% when liabilities shrank the
  denominator).

  (iii) Testing, docs, screenshots

  - 115 backend tests (added AI fact-routing regression tests) + 8 e2e, ruff +
  tsc clean.
  - Verified the smarter answers live against qwen3.6.
  - Refreshed Home/News screenshots (showing the new refresh buttons) +
  CHANGELOG; dashboard rebuilt.

  Update the Pi with cd ~/LedgerFrame && ./scripts/update.sh. Tip:
  qwen3.6-fast:latest gave noticeably quicker replies than qwen3.6:latest in my
  testing, with the same quality — worth trying since you have it pulled.

● All three done and v1.1.1 is released:
  https://github.com/gopalasubramanium/LedgerFrame/releases/tag/v1.1.1

  (i) Ask — sophisticated loading UX

  The Ask panel no longer feels dead while waiting. Now, the instant you ask:
  - An animated "thinking" indicator (pulsing dots) appears with a staged 
  message — "Gathering your portfolio data" → "Analyzing with the AI model" —
  and a live elapsed timer (· 33s).
  - After a few seconds it adds "Local/reasoning models can take a little longer
  — hang tight" (perfect for your qwen).
  - The answer streams with a blinking caret, and a Stop button lets you cancel.
  - The input auto-focuses so you can just type.

  The refreshed screenshot shows it mid-analysis with the grounding facts
  already listed.

  (ii) Keyboard PIN entry

  The PIN screen now accepts your physical keyboard — digits type, Backspace
  deletes, Enter submits — in addition to the on-screen keypad (with a hint line
  saying so). It was previously mouse/touch only; now both work.

  Bonus: fixed a real crash I caught while testing

  Capturing the Ask screenshot surfaced a genuine concurrency bug — parallel
  dashboard requests refreshing the same symbol collided with "UNIQUE constraint
  failed: quotes.instrument_id" and returned 500 ("Unable to load dashboard").
  I made the quote write an atomic SQLite upsert and instrument creation
  race-safe; hammering 30 concurrent requests now returns all 200s, zero errors.

  (iii) Testing, docs, screenshots

  - 115 backend + 8 e2e green, ruff + tsc clean.
  - Verified the new Ask UX live against your qwen3.6, and the keyboard PIN
  flow.
  - Refreshed the Ask screenshot, CHANGELOG; added a reusable
  frontend/scripts/ask_shots.mjs; dashboard rebuilt.

  Update the Pi with cd ~/LedgerFrame && ./scripts/update.sh. The reduced-motion
  accessibility setting is respected — the animations disable when that's on.

✻ Cogitated for 30m 52s

※ recap: We're building/polishing LedgerFrame, a Raspberry Pi financial dashboard; the latest work shipped v1.1.1 with the animated Ask "thinking" state, keyboard PIN entry, and a quote-write race fix. Next: update the Pi (./scripts/update.sh) and confirm the Ask panel and PIN keyboard work for you.
